    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491327487p2/1762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288990671?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=lqbtqia">lqbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=murica">murica</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288990671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8550100703278547199">I will start off by saying that I am a cis woman, and therefore my review is limited to my own experiences. <br/><br/>I love being a woman. It is a huge part of who I am, and I would be devastated if tomorrow someone told me I had to be a man because that's who I really was. My heart breaks for trans people when I think about the incredible amount of difficulties they face, simply for being themselves. And the amount of people who can't be themselves due to fear for their own safety.<br/><br/>As many more before me</span>
  <span id="freeText8550100703278547199" style="display:none">I will start off by saying that I am a cis woman, and therefore my review is limited to my own experiences. <br /><br />I love being a woman. It is a huge part of who I am, and I would be devastated if tomorrow someone told me I had to be a man because that's who I really was. My heart breaks for trans people when I think about the incredible amount of difficulties they face, simply for being themselves. And the amount of people who can't be themselves due to fear for their own safety.<br /><br />As many more before me have said, this is a really important book. It's a debut, the writing is rather sweet, the story moves a bit too quickly, and many of the characters are one dimensional (I was nearly halfway through the book before I was finally able to differentiate between Layla, Anna, and Chloe). There is also a heavy dose of 'Murica (the promposal scene, the twangy, Southern dialect, and the religious undertones - Anna's parents having an "I can't help if I'm a homophobe, I was born that way! bumper sticker triggered me way too hard in regards to how freaked out I am by the vast amount of people who think this way in the states). Despite all that, the story itself is good and it is IMPORTANT and its sheer existence is necessary. I think this would be a particularly valuable novel for younger teens between the ages of 13-16. <br /><br />Stand out moments for me were the relationship between Amanda and her parents, trying to be supportive while desperately fearing for their child's safety and ability to lead a "normal" life; as well as the confession scene between Amanda and Bee wherein Bee wonders what is okay for her to inquire about and Amanda tells her exactly what she doesn't want to be asked. This was super informative and really good to know! Parts of the novel are heart-wrenching, and I think so many people, regardless of gender or identity, would be able to take something away from this story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8550100703278547199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2907975073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2907975073" />
    <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52488949-lia"><img alt="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577875952p2/52488949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2907975073?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="user" itemprop="url" name="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" href="/user/show/52488949-lia">˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52488949-lia?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2907975073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11737483338944202963"><i> “i had been waiting my whole life for my father to want me, for him to want his daughter.” </i><br/><br/>first of all, i would like to thank meredith russo for writing this incredible book. it was quick and easy to read while still tackling important topics, and the way it was done was just amazing. you could really be laughing and smiling at the occuring events one moment, but feel broken at the heart-wrenching things the next moment. it’s important to mention that this book has been written by a trans woma</span>
  <span id="freeText11737483338944202963" style="display:none"><i> “i had been waiting my whole life for my father to want me, for him to want his daughter.” </i><br /><br />first of all, i would like to thank meredith russo for writing this incredible book. it was quick and easy to read while still tackling important topics, and the way it was done was just amazing. you could really be laughing and smiling at the occuring events one moment, but feel broken at the heart-wrenching things the next moment. it’s important to mention that this book has been written by a trans woman herself as well! we love and support all of these incredible women in this house.<br /><br />amanda was a lovely protagonist that has been through a lot, which becomes especially obvious in the flashbacks scattered throughout the book from the time when she wasn’t yet aware of her identity and before she realized that she was, indeed, a girl. we get to see how these events have shaped her to become the person she is now, and what she has learned or how she is still affected by all these things. when it comes to the side characters such as her friends though, i felt like they weren’t fleshed out enough. all the people in her friend group kind of became one and the same person for me, as i wasn’t really able to tell them apart or know what made them special. a character could be mentioned halfway through the book and i’d be like <i>wait, who now?</i> i really did like her parents and their support towards their daughter, because regardless of them loving her because she’s their child and them just wanting the best for her, you could also really see how they cope with everything and experience the situation from their perspective too.<br /><br />on another note, i didn’t think the story had to take that turn towards the ending, since it felt more like that part was written to be important rather than anything else. the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[unnecessarily cruel outing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was something that i honestly figured was coming (and from what i can tell, other reviewers have felt the same), but can i be real for a second? as a cis woman that part wanted to make me throw up over and over again, and i don’t think young trans people would love to read about it just because something educational was supposed to come out of it. i do understand where the author was coming from, buti gladly could have passed on that.<br /><br />all in all, i really enjoyed reading about amanda and her journey to becoming the person she really is and who she wants to be. and please, read the author’s note at the end of the book. if the ending didn’t make me sad enough already, that part actually made me bawl my eyes out and i had to sit still for a while and think about it before being able to just slightly move on.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>→ 4 stars</i>
</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1735848509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735848509" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735848509?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735848509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13070562014749263371">I kept hearing about this book and decided I needed to read it too. In some ways I believe it's a first - a YA novel about a transgender teen, written by a transgender author, and even the cover model is a transperson from what I understand. Crossing boundaries like crazy.<br/><br/>On other levels it is a pretty "typical" teen novel, in the sense that Amanda discovers that she is not the only one with secrets, not the only one living with high stakes should those secrets be uncovered, and the surrounding </span>
  <span id="freeText13070562014749263371" style="display:none">I kept hearing about this book and decided I needed to read it too. In some ways I believe it's a first - a YA novel about a transgender teen, written by a transgender author, and even the cover model is a transperson from what I understand. Crossing boundaries like crazy.<br /><br />On other levels it is a pretty "typical" teen novel, in the sense that Amanda discovers that she is not the only one with secrets, not the only one living with high stakes should those secrets be uncovered, and the surrounding society is brutal, unforgiving, and slow to change. These truths do not make her life any easier, but does serve to put them in context. After all, she has had to relocate to a small town near Chattanooga from a suburb of Atlanta after experiencing difficulties remaining in the same school after a suicide attempt as well as during her transition. And we all know that the south remains the one of the unfriendliest places for violence toward the transgender community. There have been <a href="http://www.hrc.org/resources/violence-against-the-transgender-community-in-2016" rel="nofollow noopener">many instances of violence committed just this year</a>. This is not just general bullying, this can be life or death.<br /><br />The author acknowledges the issues with her own novel, so I don't need to mention them (but will!) - the fact that the main character has relatively smooth sailing because she "passes" (even though there are issues with this word) and many trans people don't have this luxury. Nor do most people have options for surgeries and hormonal treatments so early, should they choose them. And obviously her family as described would not be likely to afford them. But the author allows for these things to be possible and true for a very important reason - to show Amanda as a possibility. I ended up agreeing with these decisions because I was thinking back to novels like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52258.The_Price_of_Salt" title="The Price of Salt by Patricia Highsmith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Price of Salt</a> (you may know it as Carol) where it seemed like even Patricia Highsmith <i>with</i> a pseudonym still had to have her character who dared to entertain the idea of happiness with a nonhetero sexuality end up with some kind of trauma or downfall because of it. In other words for so long, lgbt characters are only "allowed" to exist in literature if their very existence leads to negative dramatic events. Intended or not, this ends up sending a message that you must suffer to be who you are. I think the author is hoping for a time where this doesn't have to be the assumption, but had to write it to have it exist in YA literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13070562014749263371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2455901727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455901727" />
    <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda"><img alt="Rachel Aranda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585436207p2/43622386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455901727?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Aranda" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda">Rachel Aranda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38313328-if-i-was-your-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=library-rentals">library-rentals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455901727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16545822940399212533">“If I Was Your Girl” by Meredith Russo has to be one of the most complicated books I’ve had to review this year. There is no doubt that the theme of trans people being accepted as normal is important for everyone to learn. I also liked that even though one of the characters, Anna, comes from a super religious family and thinks that struggles with the “metaphysics” of the LGBTQA+ community that she still loves her friends who are apart of that community. This is an important lesson that I feel ev</span>
  <span id="freeText16545822940399212533" style="display:none">“If I Was Your Girl” by Meredith Russo has to be one of the most complicated books I’ve had to review this year. There is no doubt that the theme of trans people being accepted as normal is important for everyone to learn. I also liked that even though one of the characters, Anna, comes from a super religious family and thinks that struggles with the “metaphysics” of the LGBTQA+ community that she still loves her friends who are apart of that community. This is an important lesson that I feel everyone needs to understand as I feel that God is love and would never punish anyone for being true to themselves if it wasn’t physically harming others or forcing a person into a bad situation. The utilization of flashbacks and current events in Andrew/Amanda’s lives was utilized very well.<br /><br />Many people have said they don’t like how simplified the story is but I kind of liked this aspect as it gave people the option to think of those they know personally. If it had been too specific then it might not have connected to a wide audience and a debut YA novel tends to need to reach many people. With this in mind, I was a bit disappointed in how typical this book was. There are so many middle grade and YA stories dealing with these events (bullying, hiding one’s past when moving to new location, finding romance with a seemingly perfect yet mysterious guy, etc.) that helped make up the plot it would have been a little redundant. Still I was hoping this book would have another layer to the storyline that hadn’t been done yet and would make it more unique.<br /><br />“It I Was Your Girl” is a quick and easy read that can be emotional at times. I look forward to the day when kids and teens can read books about this topic and see that they’re normal. Also, seeing that their careers aren’t limited as this book has a trans author, model, and audio narrator. I recommend people read this story if you’re interested in getting to understand or support the trans community in some way.<br /><br />Overall, I’d rate this book somewhere between 3.75 to 4 stars. It wasn’t the best YA book I’ve ever read but it’s an important read that I did enjoy. My rating is 3.75 stars now but may be rounded up over time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16545822940399212533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HkOOBClA6A/wf9bFCevn7I0zTY/AZ/SfFbtg5sPfT7EQyuQAx8G8AlPJ/uyGkEhOA8eLZ0qziG7yXGUsFIPzRw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6Bg5p2PEi90vzXNyZXjwnyi+QSAC0b2MuPFNG33a82DmkVOjjUXf0Ix7W1vqA189pkqHyIgFwX1fFkjRqoZPlg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1606034271608672738">MEREDITH RUSSO lives in Brooklyn with her cat Shadow and probably more books than is responsible for a New York apartment. When she isn't upsetting Yankees by smiling and making eye contact on the 3 train she spends her time lifting weights, playing fighting games, blowing up the mic at karaoke, glancing anxiously at her TBR pile, and, of course, working on her next book.<br/><br/>Meredith's debut novel, If</span>
  <span id="freeText1606034271608672738" style="display:none">MEREDITH RUSSO lives in Brooklyn with her cat Shadow and probably more books than is responsible for a New York apartment. When she isn't upsetting Yankees by smiling and making eye contact on the 3 train she spends her time lifting weights, playing fighting games, blowing up the mic at karaoke, glancing anxiously at her TBR pile, and, of course, working on her next book.<br /><br />Meredith's debut novel, If I Was Your Girl, released in 2016 to rave reviews and multiple awards. Her second novel, Birthday, came out in 2019. Both novels explore themes of gender identity, sexuality, poverty, trauma, and mental illness in Southern Appalachia, though they're lighter and way less bummer-y than that list might imply. Her essays and shorter fiction can be found in The New York Times, Elle, Meet Cute, (Don't) Call Me Crazy, Radical Hope: Letters of Love and Resistance in Dangerous Times, and Out Now: Queer We Go Again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1606034271608672738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
